## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics (classical mechanics)
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving). The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, damping, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Pendulum-like oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (driven linear with damping)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Cubic damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 (velocity-cubed damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (cross-coupled nonlinearity)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — use odd polynomial in x
- Velocity-dependent terms with even powers of x (e.g., (1-x²)*v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping (limit cycle behavior)
- If acceleration has no explicit time dependence, the system is autonomous — try formulas with only x and v
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms added to the restoring/damping expression
- Position-velocity cross terms like x*v or x²*v indicate energy-exchange nonlinearities common in self-excited oscillators
- Rational restoring forces x/(1+c*x²) can model softening springs with bounded force at large displacement
- Parametric excitation manifests as multiplicative coupling between x and periodic functions of t
- Sign-preserving nonlinear damping (v*|v| or v³) models aerodynamic or fluid drag forces on oscillators
